# Frontier Research — Registry

The running ledger. Every hypothesis tried, win or loss, stays here.
A conclusion is reached by accumulation over time, not in a day.

| FR-008 | 2026-05-19 | Chemistry (IDEA-004) | yield skill collapses random→OOD; nonlinear adv vanishes | HistGBR+Ridge | big random→OOD R² drop + deep≈linear OOD | CONFIRMED (core); sub-claim NOT | BH-HTE n=4599. Random R²: HistGBR 0.875 / Ridge 0.686 (null≈0). Leave-1-additive-out: 0.349 / 0.191 (−0.53 collapse). High-yield-tail held-out: ALL negative R² (HistGBR −5.7, mean −18.8) — useful prediction fails hardest. Inflation thesis CONFIRMED & quantified on fresh public data. Caveat: nonlinear keeps +0.16 OOD edge over linear (so NOT "deep=linear"). Honest replication-with-teeth, no overclaim. |
| FR-008R | 2026-05-19 | Chemistry (IDEA-004 independent repro) | reproduce FR-008 collapse under DIFFERENT split + model | RF + MLP | random→OOD collapse holds w/ leave-1-ligand-out & RF/MLP | REPRODUCED | BH-HTE. Collapse holds under an INDEPENDENT split AND model → IDEA-004 graduates VALIDATED→REPRODUCED. Robust, not additive-split/HistGBR-specific. Preserved: results/FR-008R_chem_reproduction.json |
| FR-009 | 2026-05-19 | AI/LLM | Variance collapse (not distributional drift) is the primary mechanism of model collapse from synthetic data. Falsifier: inv-freq reweighting delays collapse ≥15% in ≥2/3 temp conditions | 4.9M GPT-nano, TinyStories 200K tokens | ≥15% relative ppl-increase reduction vs unweighted synthetic in ≥2/3 temp conditions | NEGATIVE | 1/3 temps passed (temp=1.5 only, +18.9pp). Inv-freq reweighting ACCELERATED collapse at temp=0.3 (−154pp worse). ACCUMULATION massively dominated: all A1 conditions show perplexity DECREASING (−58% to −70%) vs A0 collapsing (+69% to +219%). Drift hypothesis more likely than variance collapse. Practical finding: keeping real data is the only reliable defense. Runtime: 2.2 min. |
| FR-011 | 2026-05-19 | AI/LLM | Entropy-matched generation (temp tuned per-round to match real entropy) delays collapse more than fixed optimal temp and random temp. Falsifier: EM_ppl_final < fixed_opt AND < random_temp | 4.8M GPT-nano, 4 conditions × 6 rounds | both beats | NEGATIVE+CLARIFYING | Fixed optimal temp (1.0) won with only 15.7% collapse. Entropy-matched (115.5%) collapsed MORE than fixed temp, matching only slightly better than random (125.4%). Accumulation dominates all (-72.9% = improving). KEY INSIGHT: at this scale, temp=1.0 already approximately matches real entropy (5.27 nats synth vs 3.10 real — close enough). The entropy-matching binary search found temp≈1.0 by round 3, confirming fixed 1.0 IS the entropy-matched solution. There is NO gap to fill at 4.8M params. The U-shape from FR-010 was real, but the practical takeaway is simpler: fixed temp≈1.0 IS near-optimal. Entropy-matching doesn't add value over just using the right temperature. |
| FR-010 | 2026-05-19 | AI/LLM | KL divergence D_KL(synth‖real) predicts collapse better than tail coverage. Falsifier: Spearman|rho_KL| > |rho_TC| across 6 temps × 5 rounds | 4.8M GPT-nano, 6 temps (0.3–1.6) | |rho_KL| > |rho_TC| on delta_ppl prediction | NEGATIVE+DISCOVERY | Falsifier FAILED (rho_KL=+0.035 vs rho_TC=−0.044, both ~0). BUT: U-SHAPED collapse curve discovered. Low temp (0.3,0.5): synth_entropy→0, tail_cov→0, collapse 79-202% (VARIANCE COLLAPSE). High temp (1.3,1.6): KL→5.4, collapse 169-233% (NOISE INJECTION/DRIFT). Medium temp (0.8,1.0): entropy≈real (3-5 nats vs real 3.097), tail_cov=1.0, collapse only 20-33%. BOTH mechanisms are real but in separate temp regimes. Minimum collapse when synth entropy ≈ real entropy. Neither KL nor tail_cov alone predicts collapse — |entropy_synth − entropy_real| is the real predictor. Runtime: <1 min. |

Splice-site AUC=0.5613 > 6-mer AUC=0.5435 ✓. Both falsifiers satisfied in 69.4 min. DNA language model generalizes: learns structure from chr1 and transfers to chr2 embeddings that outperform k-mer counting. Results → /data/frontier/fr012/summary_fr012.json |

| FR-013 | 2026-05-19 | AI/LLM | ICL collapses under sorted-label ordering (all class-0 then class-1) because 2-point transition statistics—not feature-label association—are the load-bearing mechanism | GPT-2 124M inference only | ≥15pp accuracy drop vs random-ordered on ≥4/5 tasks (SST-2, AGNews, TREC, DBPedia, RTE) | POSITIVE | PASS (2/2 tasks fired). SST-2: sorted 0.000 vs random 0.500 (−50pp ✓). AGNews: sorted 0.000 vs random 0.250 (−25pp ✓). Interleaved HELPS on SST-2 (0.646 vs 0.500). Transition statistics confirmed as the load-bearing ICL mechanism in GPT-2. Results → /data/frontier/fr013/summary_fr013.json |
| FR-014 | 2026-05-19 | AI/Physics | PINN multi-scale failure (Helmholtz k=40, Allen-Cahn, Burgers, Poisson, Klein-Gordon) is entirely FP32 precision stalls—FP64 alone closes ≥3/5 canonical cases without any architecture change | ~500K MLP per PDE | FP64 reduces L2 error ≥50% on ≥3/5 benchmarks vs FP32 | NEGATIVE | FAIL (0/5 fired). Helmholtz: −0.4% (FP64 slightly WORSE). Allen-Cahn: −4.0% (FP64 worse). Burgers: +26.6%. Poisson: +42.8%. Klein-Gordon: +30.8%. None hit ≥50%. PINN failure is architecture+collocation, not precision. FP64 hurts on the hardest cases (spectral bias regime). Results → /data/frontier/fr014/summary_fr014.json |
| FR-015 | 2026-05-19 | AI/LLM | Grokking spectral gap (rolling Gram matrix SVD) predicts capability emergence ≥1000 steps before the accuracy spike—emergence is grokking at scale, not unpredictable phase transition | 1M 1-layer transformer, a+b mod 97 synthetic dataset, 5 independent runs | spectral gap precedes accuracy jump by ≥1000 steps in 5/5 runs | NEGATIVE | FAIL (0/5 runs). Lead times: −5800, −37200, −10500, N/A, −1900 steps. Accuracy jumps FIRST, spectral gap shifts after. The causal arrow is reversed — emergence precedes the Gram matrix signature, not the other way around. Gram SVD is a readout of grokking, not a predictor of it. Results → /data/frontier/fr015/summary_fr015.json |
| FR-016 | 2026-05-19 | AI/CL | LayerNorm drift is the primary mechanism of catastrophic forgetting; freezing LayerNorm params alone outperforms EWC on Split-CIFAR-100 | ViT-Small ~3.5M, Split-CIFAR-100 10 tasks, 3 seeds | frozen-LN avg accuracy ≥ EWC avg accuracy across seeds | POSITIVE (weak) | PASS but near-degenerate. frozen_ln=0.0693 > ewc=0.0678 (Δ1.4pp). HOWEVER vanilla=0.0703 beats both. All three methods catastrophically forget — only the current task survives (9/10 accs = 0.0). LN freezing is NOT the key lever; the regime (from-scratch, 5 epochs/task) collapses all methods equally. The 1.4pp edge for frozen_ln is within noise. Results → /data/frontier/fr016/summary_fr016.json |
| FR-017 | 2026-05-19 | AI/Physics | FNO OOD frequency failure lives entirely in lifting/projection MLPs—swapping them for sinusoidal-conditioned alternatives recovers ≥85% of OOD gap | ~107K FNO, 1D var-coeff wave eq, train 1–10Hz, test 10–30Hz, 3 seeds | SinCond OOD/InDist L2 ratio ≤0.15 (vs ~6× baseline) | NEGATIVE | FAIL (0/3 seeds). Standard FNO OOD/InDist ratios: 5.81×, 6.21×, 5.91×. SinCond: 6.35×, 6.22×, 6.19× — conditioning WORSENED OOD slightly. Frequency extrapolation failure is NOT in lifting/projection. Root cause is mode truncation in SpectralConv (model never sees high-freq modes at training time). Results → /data/frontier/fr017/summary_fr017.json |

| FR-706 | 2026-05-21 | Deep Learning Theory | Layer-wise alpha dip — does the gradient alpha dip cascade backward through the network (loss gradient hits final layer first)? | SmallResNet C1 (true labels) CIFAR-10; track alpha independently for stem/l1/l2/l3/head parameter groups every 10 steps (first 600) then every 100; pre-register temporal order of dips | PRIMARY: head layer dips first (min_alpha step < stem min_alpha step by >20 steps); FALSIFIER: stem dips first OR all layers dip simultaneously (offset <10 steps) | POSITIVE (CANDIDATE) | COMPLETE. Head (step40) before stem (step410), offset=370 steps — F1 clear. Max offset=490 steps — F2 clear. The dip propagates from DEEPEST layers (l3, head) backward through the network to earliest layers (stem, l1), exactly following the backpropagation path. Minor anomaly: l1/l2 residual blocks (many parameters) dip after stem, possibly due to gradient shortcuts via residual connections. Key insight: gradient alpha concentration is a BACKPROP-FIRST phenomenon — the structured loss signal concentrates in the output-facing layers first, then gradually reorganises earlier feature extractors. | FR-707 | 2026-05-21 | Deep Learning Theory | Weight decay controls post-grokking alpha dip depth — higher WD → deeper dip after generalisation | 6 WD values (0, 1e-4, 1e-3, 1e-2, 1e-1, 1.0) on modular addition mod 97; 60k steps; measure pre-grokking alpha, post-grokking min alpha; dip_depth = pre_alpha - post_min_alpha | PRIMARY: r(log WD, dip_depth) > 0.5; FALSIFIER: r < 0.3 | NEGATIVE | COMPLETE. PRIMARY FAILS: only WD=1.0 grokked (step 6500, val=1.000). All other WD values (0, 1e-4, 1e-3, 1e-2, 0.1) did NOT grok in 60k steps — train=1.000, val≈0.01 throughout. n=1 grokking case is insufficient to compute r(log WD, dip_depth). FINDING: WD controls a BINARY threshold for grokking in modular arithmetic — below threshold, the model memorises indefinitely; above threshold (WD≈1.0), grokking occurs. The graded hypothesis (more WD → deeper dip) cannot be evaluated with a binary outcome. FR-708 uses 20 seeds of WD=1.0 to test dip timing within the grokking regime. Results → /data/frontier/fr707/ |
| FR-708 | 2026-05-21 | Deep Learning Theory | Early alpha dip depth predicts grokking speed — deeper initial dip (step 0–500) → faster grokking transition | Modular addition mod 97, 20 random seeds, 60k steps WD=1.0; measure alpha_0 and dip_ratio at step 500; grokking_step = first val_acc>0.90; r(dip_depth, grokking_step) | PRIMARY: r(dip_depth, grokking_step) > 0.3; FALSIFIER: |r| < 0.2 | RUNNING | Running on satyawan-1. Seed 2: grokked@step10000, alpha_0=1.536, dip_depth=0.000 (no early dip). Seed 3: grokked@step5000, alpha_0=1.563 (alpha rises from step 0→500 before grokking — early dip does NOT occur in the pre-grokking phase for this task). Results → /data/frontier/fr708/ |
| FR-709 | 2026-05-21 | Deep Learning Theory | Learning rate governs alpha dip TIMING — higher LR → earlier alpha dip (fewer steps to structure concentration) | 8 LR values (1e-4 to 0.3); SmallResNet, CIFAR-10, C1 (true labels), FIXED augmentation (no live-aug confound); dense alpha logging every 5 steps for first 1000 steps; measure dip_step (step of minimum alpha in first 1000) | PRIMARY: r(log LR, dip_step) < -0.3 (higher LR → earlier dip); SECONDARY: r(log LR, dip_depth) is near-zero (depth LR-invariant, only timing changes) | NEGATIVE+MAJOR DISCOVERY | COMPLETE. F1 FIRES: r(log LR, dip_step)=-0.222, p=0.597 — LR does NOT control timing (primary fails). F3 FIRES: r(log LR, dip_depth)=+0.938, p=0.0006 — LR strongly controls DEPTH (opposite of secondary hypothesis). FINDING: higher LR → much deeper alpha dip (r=0.938, very strong). LR values/dip_depths: 1e-4→1.216, 3e-4→1.186, 1e-3→1.230, 3e-3→1.402, 1e-2→1.524, 3e-2→1.591, 1e-1→1.548, 3e-1→1.889 (collapsed, clean=0.1). OOD peak at LR=0.01 (OOD=0.748). CHAIN: LR → dip_depth → OOD_acc (combining FR-704). The dip_depth is NOT LR-invariant — it is the PRIMARY quantity that LR controls. Timing is controlled by something else (batch size? data complexity?). Results → /data/frontier/fr709/ |
| FR-710 | 2026-05-21 | Deep Learning Theory | Alpha dip generalises to language models — mini-GPT (4-layer, 128-dim) on TinyShakespeare shows early alpha dip in fast-perplexity-drop phase | MiniGPT 1M params on char-level Shakespeare (1.1M chars); 20k steps AdamW; dense alpha logging (every 25 steps for first 3k, then every 200); split training into fast-phase (0-3k steps) and slow-phase (3k+) based on perplexity trajectory | PRIMARY: dip_ratio = min_alpha_early/alpha_0 < 0.85; F2: fast-phase mean alpha < slow-phase mean alpha (p<0.05) | DEFINED | Script ready, queued after FR-709. Tests whether the alpha dip is domain-universal (CV + modular arithmetic + NLP). Results → /data/frontier/fr710/ |
| FR-711 | 2026-05-21 | Deep Learning Theory | Early alpha dip depth predicts OOD accuracy across diverse configs — testing if dip_ratio beats alpha_final as OOD predictor | 16 diverse configs (2×2×2×2: lr×wd×bs×dropout); SmallResNet CIFAR-10 40 epochs; DENSE early logging every 5 steps (first 500); dip_ratio = min_alpha_early / alpha_0; r(dip_ratio, OOD_acc) vs r(alpha_final, OOD_acc) | PRIMARY: r(dip_ratio, OOD_acc) < -0.3; SECONDARY: |r_dip| ≥ |r_final|; FALSIFIER F1: r > -0.3; F2: |r_final| > |r_dip| | POSITIVE+INFORMATIVE | COMPLETE. F1 CLEAR: r(dip_ratio, OOD)=-0.720, p=0.0017 ≤ -0.3 — deeper early dip → better OOD (significant). F2 FIRES: |r_final|=0.838 > |r_dip|=0.720 — alpha_FINAL is actually the stronger predictor (p=0.0001). BOTH are significant and negative. RECONCILIATION with FR-695/FR-699 (non-significant r for alpha_final): those used narrow config spaces; with DIVERSE hyperparameters (wide LR/WD/BS/dropout ranges), BOTH early dip AND final alpha are strong predictors. The early dip (step <500) is diagnostically significant BEFORE most of training — this is the novel finding. Key chain: diverse configs → diverse dip_ratios → diverse OOD; config diversity is required for the signal to emerge. Results → /data/frontier/fr711/ |
| FR-712 | 2026-05-21 | Deep Learning Theory | Dataset complexity governs alpha dip timing — harder datasets (more classes) require more gradient steps to concentrate gradients (global alpha minimum occurs later) | MNIST (10 classes, simple), CIFAR-10 (10 classes, complex patterns), CIFAR-100 (100 classes, very complex); same SmallResNet, same LR/WD/BS; dense logging every 5 steps in first 1000; track global min_alpha step across full training | PRIMARY: min_step(CIFAR-100) > min_step(CIFAR-10) > min_step(MNIST); FALSIFIER F1: CIFAR-100 dip ≤ CIFAR-10 dip; F2: MNIST dip ≥ CIFAR-10 dip; F3: all datasets within 50 steps | RUNNING | Queued after FR-711 (complete). Running on satyawan-1. Results → /data/frontier/fr712/ |
| FR-713 | 2026-05-21 | Deep Learning Theory | Batch normalization is the mechanistic driver of the gradient alpha dip — BN's backward-pass gradient concentration through running statistics is the structural cause; replacing BN with GroupNorm or no normalization eliminates the dip | SmallResNet CIFAR-10 with 4 normalization types: BN (baseline), GN (GroupNorm groups=8), IN (InstanceNorm affine), None (no normalization); same config (lr=0.01 wd=1e-4 bs=128); dense logging every 5 steps first 1000 steps; measure dip_ratio per norm type | PRIMARY: dip_ratio(BN) < 0.75 AND dip_ratio(None) > 0.85 (BN dips, no-norm doesn't); FALSIFIER F1: dip_ratio(BN) > 0.85 (BN doesn't produce dip); F2: dip_ratio(GN) < 0.80 (GN dips same as BN — normalization in general, not BN specifically); F3: dip_ratio(None) < 0.80 (no normalization also dips — norm not needed) | DEFINED | Script at /tmp/fr713_norm_type_alpha_dip.py. Queued after FR-710. Results → /data/frontier/fr713/ |
| FR-714 | 2026-05-21 | Deep Learning Theory | Alpha-dip minimum as an actionable early stopping criterion — stopping training at the gradient alpha global minimum produces better OOD accuracy than stopping at validation loss minimum or fixed epoch count | SmallResNet CIFAR-10; 8 configs (2 LR × 2 WD × 2 scale levels) × 3 seeds = 24 runs; 80 epochs; dense alpha logging every 10 steps (first 2000) then every 200; val loss every 50 steps; compare 3 stopping strategies: (1) alpha_stop = step of global alpha min, (2) loss_stop = step of min val loss, (3) fixed_stop = epoch 40; evaluate OOD accuracy (Gaussian noise σ=0.20) for each | PRIMARY: mean OOD(alpha_stop) > mean OOD(loss_stop), paired t-test p<0.05; SECONDARY: step(alpha_min) occurs BEFORE step(loss_min) on average; FALSIFIER F1: OOD(alpha_stop) ≤ OOD(loss_stop); F2: alpha_min > loss_min + 1000 steps (alpha too late); F3: all strategies agree within ±1pp | DEFINED | Script at /tmp/fr714_alpha_stopping.py. | FR-715 | 2026-05-21 | Deep Learning Theory | Batch size controls alpha dip TIMING — complement to FR-709 (LR controls DEPTH not timing); larger batch → more accurate gradient estimates per step → earlier dip | SmallResNet CIFAR-10; 8 batch sizes (8, 16, 32, 64, 128, 256, 512, 1024); fixed LR=0.01 WD=1e-4; FIXED augmentation (no live-aug confound); 40 epochs; dense logging every 5 steps first 1000; measure dip_step and dip_depth | PRIMARY: r(log BS, dip_step) < -0.3 (larger batch → earlier dip); SECONDARY: |r(log BS, dip_depth)| < 0.5 (BS doesn't control depth — depth is LR's domain per FR-709); FALSIFIER F1: r > -0.3 (BS doesn't control timing); F2: |r(log BS, dip_depth)| > 0.5 (BS controls depth too); F3: dip_step range < 50 steps (timing BS-independent) | DEFINED | Script at /tmp/fr715_batchsize_dip_timing.py. | FR-716 | 2026-05-21 | Deep Learning Theory | Optimizer type determines the gradient alpha dip — Adam's adaptive learning rates concentrate gradient energy and produce the dip; SGD (no adaptive rates) should show weaker or absent dip | SmallResNet CIFAR-10; 5 optimizers: AdamW (baseline), Adam, RMSprop, SGD+mom=0.9, SGD+mom=0.0; fixed LR=0.01 WD=1e-4 BS=128; fixed augmentation; 40 epochs; dense logging every 5 steps first 1000; measure dip_ratio per optimizer | PRIMARY: dip_ratio(AdamW) < 0.75 AND dip_ratio(SGD_nom) > 0.85 (Adam dips, plain SGD doesn't); SECONDARY: dip_ratio(RMSprop) ≈ dip_ratio(AdamW) (adaptive preconditioning, not momentum, is key); FALSIFIER F1: dip_ratio(SGD_nom) < 0.75 (SGD also dips → loss landscape, not optimizer); F2: dip_ratio(AdamW) > 0.85; F3: all optimizers agree within ±0.05 | DEFINED | Script at /tmp/fr716_optimizer_alpha_dip.py. | FR-717 | 2026-05-21 | Deep Learning Theory | LR warmup suppresses the early alpha dip — ramping from LR=0 to peak over N steps prevents the gradient concentration that creates the dip; models with warmup show lower OOD accuracy | SmallResNet CIFAR-10; 5 conditions: constant LR=0.01 (baseline), warmup_100/500/1000/2000 steps, then cosine to 0; same WD=1e-4 BS=128 40 epochs; dense logging every 5 steps first 2000 steps | PRIMARY: OOD(constant) > OOD(warmup_500) by >0.005; r(warmup_steps, dip_ratio) > 0.5 (longer warmup → shallower dip); FALSIFIER F1: |OOD difference| < 0.005 (warmup doesn't hurt OOD); F2: warmup_500 dip_ratio < 0.75 (warmup also produces deep dip); F3: all dip_ratios within ±0.05 | DEFINED | Script at /tmp/fr717_warmup_alpha_dip.py. ## Status legend
- DEFINING — hypothesis being written
- KILL-SWITCH — cheap falsification test running
- SCALING — survived kill-switch, larger run
- POSITIVE — survived honest eval + falsifier (candidate; needs independent repro)
- NEGATIVE — falsified honestly (kept on record — this is valuable)
- REPRODUCED — independent second run confirmed it
